    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_843156308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/843156308" />
    <a title="Ms.pegasus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5015851-ms-pegasus"><img alt="Ms.pegasus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335705124p2/5015851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/843156308?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms.pegasus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms.pegasus" href="/user/show/5015851-ms-pegasus">Ms.pegasus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805054088" href="/book/show/1281316.The_Book_of_Illusions">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone interested in well written fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5015851-ms-pegasus?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer843156308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11223025880022746924">A linear account of the story would disclose that David Zimmer, professor of comparative literature at a Vermont liberal arts college, lost his wife and two young sons in a tragic plane crash, and as an antidote to debilitating depression, threw himself into a study of the films of Hector Mann, an obscure comedian from the silent film era who disappeared some 60 years ago. Three months after this analytic tome was published, he received a cryptic letter from a woman named Frieda Spelling. Would </span>
  <span id="freeText11223025880022746924" style="display:none">A linear account of the story would disclose that David Zimmer, professor of comparative literature at a Vermont liberal arts college, lost his wife and two young sons in a tragic plane crash, and as an antidote to debilitating depression, threw himself into a study of the films of Hector Mann, an obscure comedian from the silent film era who disappeared some 60 years ago. Three months after this analytic tome was published, he received a cryptic letter from a woman named Frieda Spelling. Would he be interested in meeting Hector Mann? <br /><br />Fortunately, author Paul Auster has written instead a hypnotic tale that begins mid-course. He opens with the simple sentence: <i> “Everyone thought he was dead.” </i> Intriguing. This is before the “he” is identified as Hector Mann. This before Hector Mann's identity or connection with Zimmer is disclosed. What lingers after that sentence is the portent of frightening secrets and hidden motives to seduce the reader.<br /><br />The BOOK OF ILLUSIONS begins as two conjoined stories. There is Zimmer's narrative, told in first person past tense, connecting the tragedy of three years ago with the events that will unfold in the space of a few days. The other story is that of Hector Mann who feels like a ghost after that abrupt disappearance and is initially introduced through his screen persona as interpreted by Zimmer through the films he is viewing: <i> “They [the silent film comedies] were like poems, like the renderings of dreams, like some intricate choreography of the spirit, and because they were dead, they probably spoke more deeply to us now than they had to the audiences of their time.” </i> (p.15)<br /><br />Hector's story is split as well. His past is ostensibly narrated by a woman named Alma Grund who has accessed his journal. This part of the story feels like an interlude. Its purpose is to fill in the details of those 60 years and form an armature for the events to follow. The narrative fills over a fifth of the book and yet reads quickly, providing less insight and emotional depth than Zimmer's introspective examination of the films.<br /><br />Auster freely shapes the passage of time in this book to create emotional rhythms. When the films are described, he switches to the present tense. It is as if the reader is viewing the films with Zimmer and watching the ideas of his book coalesce. Time slows. The reader is lulled by Zimmer's contemplative side, an interior shell uninterrupted by the outside world. Auster counters that with a picture of derangement in an excruciating six pages detailing a disastrous dinner party. <br /><br />The book is structured like a painting built up from carefully conceived translucent layers. After completing “The Silent World of Hector Mann,” Zimmer begins a translation of Chateaubriand's posthumously published Memoirs. Alma Grund's book is being written with the understanding it will be published only after the deaths of the principals. Obsession is another element explored in this way. Alma's face is marred by a birthmark which provokes memories of Hawthorne's short story, “The Birthmark,” in which a man destroys his beloved wife by his obsession with removing her birthmark. Zimmer is unable to mute his grief except by pursuing his obsession with Hector Mann's films. Frieda Spelling harbors her own secret obsessions. The interlocking stories overlap in layers as well. A bank scene in Mann's film “The Teller” is reconfigured in a scene in Mann's journal. A ghostly romance in the film “The Inner Life of Martin Frost” feels like a variation on existential themes in Zimmer and Alma's relationship.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I had some problems with the plausibility of some of the events. After writing his book, would Zimmer have been so hesitant to follow up on Frieda Spelling's letter? After the violent hysteria of Zimmer and Grund's meeting, is it plausible that they would sleep together that very night? Was it plausible that Mann would choose to work in the sporting goods store owned by his former lover's father? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I gave this book 4 stars because of some quibbles about plausibility. However, this is one of those books that linger long after reading the final page. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11223025880022746924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6673053'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6673053-paul-auster"><img alt="Paul Auster: Moon Palace" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1327871405l/6673053._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xvZZ1gWt4L2Sd0SSJFJIL7Dftyd390b+iR+qVGWDfKFyI/eD6Q8X0/4wTEYbCPY29lMGvsdQwW2roz+8cZHpqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Az Ugrásnak nevezett jelenség<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12829864130725159345\" style=\"display:none\">Egyik pillanatról a másikra történt: 2027-ben a Nap eltűnt az égről. Helyén egy vörös törpecsillag ontja rőt fényét a Föld világos oldalára, míg a halott és fagyott sötét oldal fölött sosem látott csillagképek ragyognak. Az Ugrásnak nevezett jelenség oka ismeretlen, az emberi civilizáció beleremeg a sokkba: a napos oldali országokat menekültek milliói árasztják el, a világgazdaság összeomlik, az emberiség a túlélésért küzd. A pusztulásból azonban lassan új világ születik. Húsz év múlva a technikai fejlődés soha nem látott ütemre gyorsul, az élet friss és modern, a fiatal generációk számára a régi Föld már csak a legendákban létezik. Kerti Szófia, a genetikailag módosított budapesti lány és társai inkább a jövőbe tekintenek, ahol újabb fordulópont, a technológiai szingularitás várja az emberiséget. Egy esemény, ahol a fejlődés görbéje függőlegessé válik, amely mögé semmilyen előrejelzés nem láthat be, és ahol tudása az embert saját istenévé avathatja. De vajon valóban független-e egymástól a 2027-es Ugrás és a technikai fejlődés szédítő felgyorsulása, vagy a kozmikus színfalak mögött egy végletekig precíz kísérlet zajlik, melynek alanya maga az emberiség? A Zsoldos Péter-díjas Brandon Hackett új regényének hősei az általunk ismert emberi létezésen túl is elmerészkednek, hogy választ találjanak a rejtélyekre.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4151272134602226348">Paul Auster is the bestselling author of <em>Report from the Interior</em>, <em>Winter Journal</em>, <em>Sunset Park</em>, Invisible, <em>The Book of Illusions</em>, and <em>The New York Trilogy</em>, among many other works. He has been awarded the Prince of Asturias Prize for Literature, the Prix Médicis Étranger, the Independent Spirit Award, and the Premio Napoli. He is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters, the American Ac</span>
  <span id="freeText4151272134602226348" style="display:none">Paul Auster is the bestselling author of <em>Report from the Interior</em>, <em>Winter Journal</em>, <em>Sunset Park</em>, Invisible, <em>The Book of Illusions</em>, and <em>The New York Trilogy</em>, among many other works. He has been awarded the Prince of Asturias Prize for Literature, the Prix Médicis Étranger, the Independent Spirit Award, and the Premio Napoli. He is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters, the American Academy of Arts and Sciences, and a Commandeur de l'Ordre des Arts et des Lettres. He lives in Brooklyn, New York.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1779328-the-book-of-illusions">Quotes from The Book of Illus...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;We all want to believe in impossible things, I suppose, to persuade ourselves that miracles can happen.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/287842-we-all-want-to-believe-in-impossible-things-i-suppose">132 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I was perfectly calm and perfectly insane, perfectly prepared to accept what the moment had offered. Indifference of that magnitude is rare and because it can be achieved only by someone ready to let go of who he is, it demands respect. It inspires awe in those who gaze upon it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/748113-i-was-perfectly-calm-and-perfectly-insane-perfectly-prepared-to">34 likes</a>
            </nobr>
